href="/wiki/File:Key_Three.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Yankees\' success in the late 1990s and early 2000s was built from a <a href="/wiki/Core_Four" title="Core Four">core of productive players</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Posada" title="Jorge Posada">Jorge Posada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rivera" title="Mariano Rivera">Mariano Rivera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Joe Torre had a mediocre run as a manager in the National League,<sup id="cite_ref-JoeTorreNL_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JoeTorreNL-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and the choice was initially derided ("Clueless Joe" was a headline in the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-CluelessJoe_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CluelessJoe-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, his calm demeanor proved to be a good fit, and his tenure was the longest under George Steinbrenner\'s ownership.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1996_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1996 New York Yankees season">1996 season</a> saw the rise of three Yankees who formed the core of the team for years to come: rookie shortstop <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a>, second-year starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Andy_Pettitte" title="Andy Pettitte">Andy Pettitte</a>, and second-year pitcher <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rivera" title="Mariano Rivera">Mariano Rivera</a>, who served as <a href="/wiki/Setup_man" title="Setup man">setup man</a> in 1996 before becoming <a href="/wiki/Closer_(baseball)" title="Closer (baseball)">closer</a> in 1997. Aided by these young players, the Yankees won their first AL East title in 15 years in 1996. They defeated the <a href="/wiki/1996_Texas_Rangers_season" title="1996 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1996_American_League_Division_Series" title="1996 American League Division Series">ALDS</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/1996_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1996 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> beat the <a href="/wiki/1996_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1996 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in five games, which included a notable fan interference by young <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Maier" title="Jeffrey Maier">Jeffrey Maier</a> that was called as a home run for the Yankees. In the <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series" title="1996 World Series">World Series</a> the team rebounded from an 0\xe2\x80\x932 series deficit and defeated the defending champion <a href="/wiki/1996_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1996 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a>, ending an 18-year championship drought. Jeter was named Rookie of the Year. In 1997, the Yankees lost the <a href="/wiki/1997_American_League_Division_Series" title="1997 American League Division Series">1997 ALDS</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1997_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1997 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a> in five games. General manager <a href="/wiki/Bob_Watson" title="Bob Watson">Bob Watson</a> stepped down and was replaced by assistant general manager <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cashman" title="Brian Cashman">Brian Cashman</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">1998 Yankees</a> are widely acknowledged to be one of the greatest teams in baseball history, compiling a then-AL record 114 regular season wins against just 48 losses and then sweeping the <a href="/wiki/1998_San_Diego_Padres_season" title="1998 San Diego Padres season">San Diego Padres</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998 World Series</a>. Their 125 combined regular and postseason wins is an MLB single-season record.\n</p><p>On May 17, 1998, <a href="/wiki/David_Wells" title="David Wells">David Wells</a> pitched a <a href="/wiki/David_Wells%27_perfect_game" title="David Wells&#39; perfect game">perfect game</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1998_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1998 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a> at Yankee Stadium. On July 18, 1999, which was "Yogi Berra Day" at the stadium, <a href="/wiki/David_Cone" title="David Cone">David Cone</a> pitched a <a href="/wiki/David_Cone%27s_perfect_game" title="David Cone&#39;s perfect game">perfect game</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1999_Montreal_Expos_season" title="1999 Montreal Expos season">Montreal Expos</a>, with both Berra and <a href="/wiki/Don_Larsen" title="Don Larsen">Don Larsen</a>, the pitching battery for Larsen\xe2\x80\x99s World Series perfect game on October 8, 1956, against the Brooklyn Dodgers, in attendance. The <a href="/wiki/1999_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1999 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> was the Yankees\' first meeting with the <a href="/wiki/1999_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1999 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a> in a post-season series. The <a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1999 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> went on to win the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999 World Series</a> giving the 1998\xe2\x80\x931999 Yankees a 22\xe2\x80\x933 record (including four series sweeps) in six consecutive post-season series.\n</p><p>In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2000 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> faced the <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Mets_season" title="2000 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> in the first <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a> <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">World Series</a> since 1956. The Yankees won the series in 5 games, but a loss in Game 3 snapped their streak of World Series wins at 14, surpassing the club\'s previous record of 12 (in 1927, 1928, and 1932). The Yankees are the last major league team to repeat as World Series champions and after the 2000 season they joined the Yankee teams of 1936\xe2\x80\x931939 and 1949\xe2\x80\x931953, as well as the 1972\xe2\x80\x931974 Oakland Athletics as the only teams to win at least three consecutive World Series.\n</p><p>The Yankees dynasty of the 1990s was also part the <a href="/wiki/Braves%E2%80%93Mets_rivalry" title="Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry">Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry</a>. As noted above, three of their four World Series wins happened against either team (Braves in 1996 and 1999, Mets in 2000).<sup id="cite_ref-MetsBravesrivalry_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetsBravesrivalry-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Joe Torre added further fuel to the dynasty being part of the rivalry, having played for and managed both teams and he becoming manager of the Yankees and the events of the 1996 season were seen as factors in that rivalry intensifying.<sup id="cite_ref-MetsBravesrivalry_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetsBravesrivalry-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, that year, <a href="/wiki/2001_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2001 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/2001_Oakland_Athletics_season" title="2001 Oakland Athletics season">Oakland A\'s</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2001_American_League_Division_Series" title="2001 American League Division Series">ALDS</a>, and the Seattle Mariners in the <a href="/wiki/2001_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2001 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>. By winning the pennant for a fourth straight year, the 1998\xe2\x80\x932001 Yankees joined the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">1921\xe2\x80\x931924 New York Giants</a>, and the Yankee teams of \'36\xe2\x80\x93\'39, \'49\xe2\x80\x93\'53, \'55\xe2\x80\x93\'58 and \'60\xe2\x80\x93\'64 as the only teams to win at least four straight <a href="/wiki/Pennant_(sports)" title="Pennant (sports)">pennants</a>. The Yankees won 11 consecutive postseason series in this 4-year period. In the <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">World Series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2001_Arizona_Diamondbacks_season" title="2001 Arizona Diamondbacks season">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>, the Yankees lost the series when closer Mariano Rivera uncharacteristically blew a save in the bottom of the ninth inning of Game 7; it was the second time in five years that a team lost the World Series after taking a lead into the bottom of the ninth inning of Game 7 (following the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a>) and the first time since <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a> that the home team won all seven games of a World Series. The Yankees were also the first American League team to lose a World Series in which the home team won all seven games.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Also, despite a very poor series overall, batting under .200, Derek Jeter got the nickname, "Mr. November", echoing comparisons Reggie Jackson\'s "Mr. October", for his walk-off home run in Game 4, though it began October 31, as the game ended in the first minutes of November 1. In addition, the Yankees\' home field in the aftermath of the attacks served as hosts of a memorial service titled "Prayer for America."\n</p><p>A vastly revamped <a href="/wiki/2002_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2002 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> team finished the 2002 season with an AL best record of 103\xe2\x80\x9358. The season was highlighted by <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a> becoming the first second baseman ever to hit 30 home runs and steal 30 bases in a season. In the <a href="/wiki/2002_American_League_Division_Series" title="2002 American League Division Series">ALDS</a> the Yankees lost to the eventual champion <a href="/wiki/2002_Anaheim_Angels_season" title="2002 Anaheim Angels season">Anaheim Angels</a> in four games.\n</p><p>In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/2003_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2003 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> again had the best league record (101\xe2\x80\x9361), highlighted by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Clemens" title="Roger Clemens">Roger Clemens</a>\' 300th win and 4000th strikeout. In the <a href="/wiki/2003_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2003 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, they defeated the <a href="/wiki/2003_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2003 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> in a dramatic seven game series, which featured a bench-clearing incident in Game 3 and a series-ending <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> by <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Boone" title="Aaron Boone">Aaron Boone</a> in the bottom of the 11th inning of Game 7. In the <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">World Series</a> the Yankees lost in 6 games to the <a href="/wiki/2003_Florida_Marlins_season" title="2003 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a>, losing a World Series at home for the first time since 1981.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg/170px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg" width="170" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg/255px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg/340px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="3336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2008-04-19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yankees\' third baseman <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/2004_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2004 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, who moved to third base from his usual shortstop position to accommodate Derek Jeter. In the <a href="/wiki/2004_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2004 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, the Yankees met the <a href="/wiki/2004_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2004 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> again, and became the first team in professional baseball history, and only the third team in North American pro sports history, to lose a best-of-seven series after taking a 3\xe2\x80\x930 series lead.\n</p><p>In 2005 Alex Rodriguez won the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a> award, becoming the first Yankee to win the award since Don Mattingly in 1985. The Yankees again won the AL East by virtue of a tiebreaker but lost the <a href="/wiki/2005_American_League_Division_Series" title="2005 American League Division Series">ALDS</a> in five games to the <a href="/wiki/2005_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a>. The 2006 season was highlighted by a 5-game series sweep of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2006 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a> at Fenway Park (sometimes referred to as the "Second Boston Massacre"), outscoring the Red Sox 49\xe2\x80\x9326.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite winning the AL East for the ninth consecutive year, the Yankees lost again in the <a href="/wiki/2006_American_League_Division_Series" title="2006 American League Division Series">ALDS</a>, this time to the <a href="/wiki/2006_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2006 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a>. After the ALDS was over, tragedy struck when pitcher <a href="/wiki/Cory_Lidle" title="Cory Lidle">Cory Lidle</a> died when his <a href="/wiki/October_11,_2006_New_York_City_plane_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="October 11, 2006 New York City plane crash">plane crashed</a> into a highrise apartment building in Manhattan. Along with Thurman Munson, Lidle was the second active Yankee to be killed in a private plane crash.\n</p><p>On June 18, 2007, the Yankees broke new ground by signing the first two professional baseball players from the People\'s Republic of China to the MLB,<sup id="cite_ref-chineseplayers_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chineseplayers-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and became the first team in MLB history to sign an advertising deal with a Chinese company.<sup id="cite_ref-chineseads_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chineseads-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees\' streak of nine straight AL East division titles ended in 2007, but they still reached the playoffs with the AL Wild Card. For the third year in a row, the team lost in the first round of the playoffs, as the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2007 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a> defeated the Yankees in the <a href="/wiki/2007_American_League_Division_Series" title="2007 American League Division Series">2007 ALDS</a>. After the series, Joe Torre declined a reduced-length and compensation contract offer from the Yankees and returned to the National League as manager of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Back_on_top:_Championship_run_followed_by_struggles_.282008.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Back_on_top:_Championship_run_followed_by_struggles_(2008\xe2\x80\x932016)">Back on top: Championship run followed by struggles (2008\xe2\x80\x932016)</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg/140px-Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg" width="140" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg/210px-Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg/280px-Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2033" data-file-height="3709" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joe_Girardi_by_Keith_Allison.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Yankees catcher <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a> became manager in 2008.</div></div></div>\n<p>After Torre\'s departure the Yankees signed former catcher <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a> to a three-year contract to manage the club.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The 2008 <a href="/wiki/2008_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2008 Major League Baseball season">season</a> was the last season played at Yankee Stadium. To celebrate the final year and history of Yankee Stadium, the <a href="/wiki/2008_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2008 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2008 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a> was played there on July 15, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The final regular-season game at Yankee Stadium was played on September 21, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> After the game, Jeter addressed the crowd, thanking them for their support over the years, and urging them to "take the memories of this field, add them to the new memories that will come at the new Yankee Stadium and continue to pass them on from generation to generation."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Despite multiple midseason roster moves, the team was hampered by injuries and missed the playoffs for the first time in 14 seasons.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/220px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/330px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg/440px-Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2154" data-file-height="1616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yankee_Stadium_upper_deck_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The new Yankee Stadium opened in 2009 and was christened with a World Series victory.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2009_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2009 New York Yankees season">2009 New York Yankees season</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">2009 World Series</a></div>\n<p>During the off-season, the Yankees retooled their roster with several star free agent acquisitions, including <a href="/wiki/CC_Sabathia" title="CC Sabathia">CC Sabathia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Teixeira" title="Mark Teixeira">Mark Teixeira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/A._J._Burnett" title="A. J. Burnett">A. J. Burnett</a>. At the beginning of the 2009 season, the Yankees opened the new <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>, located just a block north on River Avenue from their former home. The Yankees set a major league record by playing error-free ball for 18 consecutive games from May 14 to June 1, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees finished first in the AL East. In the <a href="/wiki/2009_American_League_Division_Series" title="2009 American League Division Series">ALDS</a> they defeated the Twins in a sweep before moving on to the <a href="/wiki/2009_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2009 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> where the Yankees defeated <a href="/wiki/2009_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Angels</a> in six games. They defeated the <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Series" title="2008 World Series">defending champions</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2009_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2009 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, in Game 6 of the <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">World Series</a> 7\xe2\x80\x933, to take the series 4\xe2\x80\x932, their 27th World Series title.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2010 New York Yankees season">2010 New York Yankees season</a></div>\n<p>The 2010 season featured the rivalry between the Yankees and <a href="/wiki/2010_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2010 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a> being revived to start and end the season. The Yankees and the Red Sox started and finished the season against each other at Fenway Park.<sup id="cite_ref-RedSox2010_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RedSox2010-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yankees2010_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yankees2010-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> This was the first time since 1950 this had happened.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In June, Joe Torre\'s Dodgers played games against the Yankees for the first time since he became manager of the Dodgers, with the Yankees taking two out of three games in the series.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> During the 2010 All-Star break, Pennsylvania announcer <a href="/wiki/Bob_Sheppard" title="Bob Sheppard">Bob Sheppard</a> and principal owner <a href="/wiki/George_Steinbrenner" title="George Steinbrenner">George Steinbrenner</a> died. Eight days later, another longtime Yankee icon, former player and manager <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Houk" title="Ralph Houk">Ralph Houk</a>, died. The Yankees won the American League Wild Card. They swept the Minnesota Twins in the <a href="/wiki/2010_American_League_Division_Series" title="2010 American League Division Series">2010 American League Division Series</a>, but lost to the Texas Rangers in the <a href="/wiki/2010_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2010 American League Championship Series">2010 American League Championship Series</a> 4 games to 2.\n</p><p>In a 22\xe2\x80\x939 win over the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Athletics</a> at home on August 25, 2011, the Yankees became the first team in Major League history to hit three <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slams</a> in a single game. They were hit by <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Can%C3%B3" title="Robinson Can\xc3\xb3">Robinson Can\xc3\xb3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Martin" title="Russell Martin">Russell Martin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Granderson" title="Curtis Granderson">Curtis Granderson</a>. The Yankees won the AL East title for the second time in three seasons, finishing with 97 wins and took home field throughout the AL postseason. However, they were defeated by the Tigers in five games in the <a href="/wiki/2011_American_League_Division_Series" title="2011 American League Division Series">2011 American League Division Series</a>.\n</p><p>In 2012, the Yankees again finished the season with the AL\'s best record at 95\xe2\x80\x9367. In mid-July the Yankees traded two prospects to the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ichiro_Suzuki" title="Ichiro Suzuki">Ichiro Suzuki</a>. They faced the Orioles in the <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Division_Series" title="2012 American League Division Series">2012 American League Division Series</a>. In Game 3, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Iba%C3%B1ez" title="Ra\xc3\xbal Iba\xc3\xb1ez">Ra\xc3\xbal Iba\xc3\xb1ez</a> became the oldest player to hit two home runs in a game, the oldest to hit a walk-off homer, the first substitute position player in a postseason game to hit two home runs, and the first to hit two home runs in the 9th inning or later in a postseason game, in the Yankees\' 3\xe2\x80\x932 win. The Yankees defeated the Orioles in five games. But in the <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2012 American League Championship Series">2012 American League Championship Series</a>, the Yankees lost to the Tigers again, this time in a four-game sweep, which was compounded with a struggling offense and a season-ending injury to Derek Jeter.\n</p><p>The 2013 season was riddled with injuries. Mark Teixeira strained his elbow during the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">WBC</a> and played only 15 games in the season, Alex Rodriguez played only 44 games after a hip surgery, Derek Jeter played only 17 games due to his ankle injury from the 2012 ALCS and Curtis Granderson played only 61 games due to forearm and knuckle injuries. On April 12, 2013, the Yankees made their second <a href="/wiki/Triple_play" title="Triple play">triple play</a> ever in a home game playing the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>. It was scored as 4\xe2\x80\x936\xe2\x80\x935\xe2\x80\x936\xe2\x80\x935\xe2\x80\x933\xe2\x80\x934, the first triple play of its kind in baseball history.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On September 25, 2013, the Yankees lost to the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a>, which for the second time in the wild card era, eliminated them from any playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> They ended the season 85-77, finishing in 3rd place in the AL East.\n</p><p>During the 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 off-season, the Yankees went on a large free agent spending spree, signing players such as <a href="/wiki/Brian_McCann_(baseball)" title="Brian McCann (baseball)">Brian McCann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacoby_Ellsbury" title="Jacoby Ellsbury">Jacoby Ellsbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masahiro_Tanaka" title="Masahiro Tanaka">Masahiro Tanaka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a>. Despite that, the Yankees missed the playoffs for the second straight season, the first time in the post-1994 strike era, finishing 2nd in the AL East with an 84-78 record. Rodriguez missed the entire season due to a 162-game suspension for his participation in the <a href="/wiki/Biogenesis_baseball_scandal" title="Biogenesis baseball scandal">Biogenesis baseball scandal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> One notable moment happened on September 25, 2014, when Derek Jeter \xe2\x80\x93 playing his final home game \xe2\x80\x93 hit a walk-off single off pitcher <a href="/wiki/Evan_Meek" title="Evan Meek">Evan Meek</a> to defeat the Baltimore Orioles in front of 48,613 fans who came to see the captain for the last time.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Reliever <a href="/wiki/Dellin_Betances" title="Dellin Betances">Dellin Betances</a> finished 3rd in voting for <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">AL Rookie of the Year</a>, while starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Masahiro_Tanaka" title="Masahiro Tanaka">Masahiro Tanaka</a> finished 5th.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2015_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2015 New York Yankees season">2015 season</a> saw the Yankees make the playoffs for the first time since 2012. In his return from suspension, Rodriguez hit 33 home runs, his most since 2008, and tied Hank Aaron\'s record of fifteen 30-homer seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Teixeira hit 31 home runs before a hit-by-pitch ended his season in August. Rookie first baseman <a href="/wiki/Greg_Bird_(baseball)" title="Greg Bird (baseball)">Greg Bird</a> had an impressive showing in Teixeira\'s place, hitting 11 home runs in 46 games, while rookie starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Luis_Severino" title="Luis Severino">Luis Severino</a> went 5-3 with a 2.89 ERA in 62.1 innings after getting called up in August. Closer <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Miller_(baseball)" title="Andrew Miller (baseball)">Andrew Miller</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Reliever_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Reliever of the Year Award">AL Reliever of the Year Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees led the AL East for most of the year before being felled by a surging Toronto Blue Jays team, ending the season 87-75 and in 2nd place. They were soundly defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a>, 3\xe2\x80\x930 in the <a href="/wiki/2015_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2015 American League Wild Card Game">2015 American League Wild Card Game</a>, shutout for six innings by opposing starter <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Keuchel" title="Dallas Keuchel">Dallas Keuchel</a>, earning boos from the frustrated home crowd of Yankees fans.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the off-season, the Yankees traded for <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>\' closer <a href="/wiki/Aroldis_Chapman" title="Aroldis Chapman">Aroldis Chapman</a> after a domestic violence allegation lowered his value. Chapman was later suspended 30 games.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees started the <a href="/wiki/2016_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2016 New York Yankees season">2016 season</a> on a rough note, starting 9-17. The resurgent 2015 experienced by Rodriguez and Teixeira did not carry over, as they batted .200 and .204 for the season, respectively. Bird was ruled out for the season after undergoing shoulder surgery. Starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Michael_Pineda" title="Michael Pineda">Michael Pineda</a> struggled, going 6-12 with a 4.82 ERA, the 7th-highest in baseball. At the <a href="/wiki/Trade_deadline" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade deadline">trade deadline</a>, the Yankees stood at an uninspiring 52-52, persuading ownership to trade away their most valuable assets and be sellers at the deadline.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_Era:_Baby_Bombers_.282017.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Era:_Baby_Bombers_(2017\xe2\x80\x93present)">New Era: Baby Bombers (2017\xe2\x80\x93present)</span></h3>\n<p>On July 25, 2016, the Yankees traded Aroldis Chapman to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> for a group of players that included top shortstop prospect <a href="/wiki/Gleyber_Torres" title="Gleyber Torres">Gleyber Torres</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and traded Andrew Miller to the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> for prospects outfielder <a href="/wiki/Clint_Frazier" title="Clint Frazier">Clint Frazier</a> and pitcher <a href="/wiki/Justus_Sheffield" title="Justus Sheffield">Justus Sheffield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the Yankees traded 39-year-old designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Beltran" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Beltran">Carlos Beltran</a> to the Texas Rangers for minor league prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees\' decision to be "sellers" rather than "buyers" at the trade deadline (trading established, veteran players for young prospects) was unusual, given the Yankees\' typical win-now approach. In discussing the midseason trades, Yankees general manager Brian Cashman said that the Yankees recognized the "need to look toward the future."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early August, both Teixeira and Rodriguez revealed their plans to retire by the season\'s end.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez played his final game on August 12.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. In his fourth-to-last game, Teixeira hit a walk-off grand slam against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, his 409th and last career home run.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The Yankees called up <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Austin" title="Tyler Austin">Tyler Austin</a> and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Judge" title="Aaron Judge">Aaron Judge</a> in August. They made their debuts on August 13, hitting back-to-back home runs in their first career at-bats.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Catcher <a href="/wiki/Gary_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Gary S\xc3\xa1nchez">Gary S\xc3\xa1nchez</a> hit 20 home runs in only 53 games, finishing 2nd in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">AL Rookie of the Year</a> voting and setting the record at the time as the fastest to reach 20 career home runs.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Sanchez, Judge and Austin, as well as the Yankees\' prosperous farm system in general, became nicknamed the "Baby Bombers".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After having traded Chapman to the Cubs during the 2016 season, the Yankees signed him as a free agent during the 2016-17 off-season; Chapman agreed to a five-year, $86 million contract, the most lucrative for a relief pitcher in history.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the Yankees finished the season with a record of 91-71. This was the first time the Yankees won 90 or more games in a season since 2012. They finished second in the AL East behind the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a>, but captured the first <a href="/wiki/AL_Wild_Card" class="mw-redirect" title="AL Wild Card">AL Wild Card</a> spot. Judge and S\xc3\xa1nchez combined for 85 home runs. Sanchez finished with 33, the most by a Yankees catcher in a single season. Judge led the American League with 52 home runs, breaking Mark McGwire\'s major league record for most home runs by a rookie in a single season (McGwire hit 49 in 1987).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees starting pitching was led by ace <a href="/wiki/Luis_Severino" title="Luis Severino">Luis Severino</a>, who rebounded from his last season to lead the Yankees\' pitching staff. On July 1, Clint Frazier made his MLB debut where he went 2 for 4 with a home run.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees sent <a href="/wiki/Dellin_Betances" title="Dellin Betances">Dellin Betances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starlin_Castro" title="Starlin Castro">Starlin Castro</a>, S\xc3\xa1nchez, Severino, and Judge to the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>. Judge won the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Home_Run_Derby_(Major_League_Baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Run Derby (Major League Baseball)">Home Run Derby</a>, making the Yankees the team with the most players to win a Home Run Derby in history.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the 2017 All-Star break, the Yankees made a series of moves to acquire third baseman <a href="/wiki/Todd_Frazier" title="Todd Frazier">Todd Frazier</a>, former Yankee reliever <a href="/wiki/David_Robertson_(baseball)" title="David Robertson (baseball)">David Robertson</a>, reliever <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Kahnle" title="Tommy Kahnle">Tommy Kahnle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> starter <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Gray" title="Sonny Gray">Sonny Gray</a>, and starter <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Garcia" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaime Garcia">Jaime Garcia</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2017_AL_Wild_Card_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 AL Wild Card Game">2017 AL Wild Card Game</a> at Yankee Stadium, the Yankees defeated the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a> 8\xe2\x80\x934 to move on the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Division_Series" title="American League Division Series">ALDS</a>; this was the Yankees\' first playoff win since 2012. In the ALDS, the Yankees lost the first two games to the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> before winning the final three games and taking the series.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> They played the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> in the 2017 <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> and lost the series in seven games.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2017 off-season, the Yankees hired <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Boone" title="Aaron Boone">Aaron Boone</a> to succeed Joe Girardi, as their new manager on December 4, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On December 11, 2017, the Yankees traded <a href="/wiki/Starlin_Castro" title="Starlin Castro">Starlin Castro</a> and prospects Jorge Guzman and Jose Devers to the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> for reigning National League Most Valuable Player <a href="/wiki/Giancarlo_Stanton" title="Giancarlo Stanton">Giancarlo Stanton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> A right fielder who bats right-handed, Stanton hit 59 home runs and drove in 132 runs--both major league highs--in 2017;<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> his contract is the largest player contract in the history of professional sports in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On December 12, the Yankees traded third baseman <a href="/wiki/Chase_Headley" title="Chase Headley">Chase Headley</a> and right-handed pitcher <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Mitchell" title="Bryan Mitchell">Bryan Mitchell</a> to the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> for outfielder <a href="/wiki/Jabari_Blash" title="Jabari Blash">Jabari Blash</a>; following the move, Yankees GM Brian Cashman stated that the trade "create[d] payroll flexibility".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>On September 28, 2018 the Yankees tied the record for the most HR\'s in a season with the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a>. On September 29, 2018 <a href="/wiki/Gleyber_Torres" title="Gleyber Torres">Gleyber Torres</a> hit the Yankees 265th home run of the season which broke the record of the most HR\'s in a season. The Yankees ended the 2018 season with a record of 100-62. With the Red Sox ending with an MLB best 108 wins. On top of that the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> ended with 103 wins, which marked the first time that three teams in one league all had 100 or more wins in a season.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctions">Distinctions</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg/170px-Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg/255px-Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg/340px-Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="754" data-file-height="352" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Champ_Ring_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/World_Series_ring" title="World Series ring">World Series rings</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_seasons" title="List of New York Yankees seasons">List of New York Yankees seasons</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="New York Yankees award winners and league leaders">New York Yankees award winners and league leaders</a></div>\n<p>The Yankees have won a record 27 World Series in 40 appearances (which, since the first World Series in 1903, currently amounts to an average appearance every 2.7 seasons and a championship every 4.0 seasons); the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> are second with 11 World Series victories. The Yankees\' number of World Series losses, 13, leads Major League Baseball. The St. Louis Cardinals, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Brooklyn/Los Angeles Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">New York/San Francisco Giants</a> are second in total World Series appearances with eighteen apiece. Of their 18 World Series appearances, the Dodgers have faced the Yankees eleven times, going 3\xe2\x80\x938, while the Giants have faced the Yankees seven times, going 2\xe2\x80\x935.<sup id="cite_ref-Dodgers_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dodgers-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Among North American major sports, the Yankees\' success is approached only by the 24 <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> championships of the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Canadiens" title="Montreal Canadiens">Montreal Canadiens</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>. The Yankees have played in the World Series against every National League pennant winner except the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WSFeat_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSFeat-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Through 2017, the Yankees have an all-time regular season winning percentage of .569 (a 10,175\xe2\x80\x937,719 record), the best of any team in baseball.<sup id="cite_ref-BestRecord_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BestRecord-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Series_championships">World Series championships</span></h2>\n<p>The Yankees have won 27 World Series Championships. Their most recent one came in 2009, under manager Joe Girardi, when they defeated the Philadelphia Phillies in six games.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series" title="1996 World Series">1996</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1996_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1996 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a></td>\n<td>4\xe2\x80\x932</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1996_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1996 New York Yankees season">92\xe2\x80\x9370</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998</a></td>\n<td>Joe Torre</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1998_San_Diego_Padres_season" title="1998 San Diego Padres season">San Diego Padres</a></td>\n<td>4\xe2\x80\x930</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">114\xe2\x80\x9348</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999</a></td>\n<td>Joe Torre</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1999_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1999 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a></td>\n<td>4\xe2\x80\x930</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1999 New York Yankees season">98\xe2\x80\x9364</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a></td>\n<td>Joe Torre</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Mets_season" title="2000 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a></td>\n<td>4\xe2\x80\x931</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2000 New York Yankees season">87\xe2\x80\x9374</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">2009</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2009_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2009 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a></td>\n<td>4\xe2\x80\x932</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2009_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2009 New York Yankees season">103\xe2\x80\x9359</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<th style="background-color:#C4CED3;color:#122448;;" colspan="4"><b>Total World Series championships:</b>\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4CED3;color:#122448;;"><b>27</b>\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_nicknames">Team nicknames</span></h2>\n<p>The "Yankees" name is often shortened to "the Yanks." Their most prominently used <a href="/wiki/List_of_baseball_nicknames" title="List of baseball nicknames">nickname</a> is "the Bronx Bombers" or simply "the Bombers", a reference to their home and their prolific hitting. A less used nickname is "the Pinstripes", in reference to the iconic feature on their home uniforms. Critics often refer to the team and the organization as "the Evil Empire", a term applied to the Yankees by <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> president <a href="/wiki/Larry_Lucchino" title="Larry Lucchino">Larry Lucchino</a> in a 2002 interview with the <i>New York Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A term from the team\'s tumultuous late 70s, "the Bronx Zoo", is sometimes used by detractors, as well as the "Damn Yankees", after the <a href="/wiki/Damn_Yankees" title="Damn Yankees">musical of the same name</a>. Ironically, even many Yankees <i>supporters</i> refer to their team as the "Evil Empire" as a badge of honor and in fact enjoy having their team play "the villain".\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Logo.2C_uniform.2C_and_dress_code"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo,_uniform,_and_dress_code">Logo, uniform, and dress code</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Logos_and_uniforms_of_the_New_York_Yankees" title="Logos and uniforms of the New York Yankees">Logos and uniforms of the New York Yankees</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popularity">Popularity</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fan_support">Fan support</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FreddySez.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FreddySez.jpg/170px-FreddySez.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FreddySez.jpg/255px-FreddySez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/FreddySez.jpg/340px-FreddySez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2142" data-file-height="2856" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FreddySez.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"<a href="/wiki/Freddy_Schuman" title="Freddy Schuman">Freddy Sez</a>" holding one of his signs near the bleachers entrance before a game between the Yankees and the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a></div></div></div>\n<p>With their recurring success since the 1920s, the Yankees have since been one of the most popular teams in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-brtop50_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brtop50-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> with their fan base coming from much further than the <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a>. The Yankees typically bring an upsurge in attendance at all or most of their various road-trip venues, drawing crowds of their own fans, as well as home-town fans whose interest is heightened when the Yankees come to town.\n</p><p>The first 1 million-fan season was in 1920, when 1,289,422 fans attended Yankee games at the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a>. The first 2 million-fan season was in 1946, when 2,265,512 fans attended the games at Yankee Stadium. The Yankees have beaten the league average for home attendance 83 out of the last 87 years (only during 1990, 1991, 1992 and 1994 did they not accomplish this). In the past seven years, the Yankees have drawn over three million fans each year, with an American League record-setting 4,090,696 in 2005, becoming only the third franchise in sports history to draw over four million in regular season attendance in their own ballpark.<sup id="cite_ref-4million_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4million-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees were the league leaders in "road attendance" each year from 2001 through 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-RoadAttendance_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RoadAttendance-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One famous fan was <a href="/wiki/Freddy_Schuman" title="Freddy Schuman">Freddy Schuman</a>, popularly known as "<b>Freddy Sez</b>." For over 50 years, he came to the Yankees\' home games with a baseball cap, a Yankees\' jersey (which on the back bears his own name), and a cake pan with a <a href="/wiki/Shamrock" title="Shamrock">shamrock</a> painted on it, which was connected to a sign inscribed with words of encouragement for the home team. Schuman died on October 17, 2010, at the age of 85.\n</p><p>To avoid unwanted publicity, Yankees members use <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">aliases</a> when registering for hotels. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> published a list of aliases used by Yankees members, and the contents were republished on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smoking_Gun" title="The Smoking Gun">The Smoking Gun</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HotelNames_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HotelNames-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bleacher_Creatures">The Bleacher Creatures</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BleacherShirt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/BleacherShirt.jpg/220px-BleacherShirt.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/BleacherShirt.jpg/330px-BleacherShirt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/BleacherShirt.jpg/440px-BleacherShirt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2856" data-file-height="2142" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BleacherShirt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A shirt worn by a number of <a href="/wiki/Bleacher_Creatures" title="Bleacher Creatures">Bleacher Creatures</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bleacher_Creatures" title="Bleacher Creatures">Bleacher Creatures</a></div>\n<p>The "Bleacher Creatures" are a notorious group of season ticket holders who occupied Section 39 in the right field bleachers at the old Yankee Stadium, and occupy Section 203 in the new one. They are known for their strict allegiance to the Yankees, and are often merciless to opposing fans who sit in the section and cheer for the road team. They enjoy taunting the opposing team\'s right fielder with a series of chanting and slandering. The "creatures" got their nickname from <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i> columnist Filip "Flip" Bondy, who spent the 2004 season sitting in the section for research on his book about the group, <i>Bleeding Pinstripes: A Season with the Bleacher Creatures of Yankee Stadium</i>, published in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="The_Judge.27s_Chambers_at_Yankee_Stadium"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Judge\'s_Chambers_at_Yankee_Stadium">The Judge\'s Chambers at Yankee Stadium</span></h3>\n<p>In 2017, team management ordered the creation of a special cheer section within Section 104 for fans of Yankees outfielder <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Judge" title="Aaron Judge">Aaron Judge</a>, called "the Judge\'s Chambers". They were the second AL team to create a special cheering section, following the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a>. The Judge\'s Chambers was added in response to his rise as one of the league\'s most popular young stars. The section\'s 18 seats are given to lucky ticketholders and their families, along with black judicial robes with the team logo on the front and Judge\'s 99 jersey number on the back; prior to the addition of the section, fans were wearing white wigs and judicial robes to games in support of Judge.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Occasionally, community organizations, charities and Little League teams are given precedence when selecting participants. The seats, which are close to his position in right field, are surrounded by mahogany wood to emulate the appearance of the city\'s courthouses.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_expansion_and_business_model">Global expansion and business model</span></h3>\n<p>The Yankees baseball club is formally owned by <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Global_Enterprises" title="Yankee Global Enterprises">Yankee Global Enterprises</a> which owns the team\'s regional YES sports network. While the club has claimed it is operating under annual losses in excess of $47 million this figure is attributed only to the ballclub\'s finances and not to finances attributed to YES or Yankees Global Enterprises.\n</p><p>The Yankees have become well known for a winning reputation on a global level. In 2007, they reached an agreement with the Chinese Baseball Association to allow coaches, scouts and trainers to work in China to promote baseball and judge talent.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> They are trying to do the same with the <a href="/wiki/Yomiuri_Giants" title="Yomiuri Giants">Yomiuri Giants</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hanshin_Tigers" title="Hanshin Tigers">Hanshin Tigers</a> in Japan. The Yankees and Yomiuri Giants currently have a close relationship and share ideas and strategies. The <a href="/wiki/Yomiuri_Shimbun" title="Yomiuri Shimbun">Yomiuri Shimbun</a> daily newspaper has an ad on the left-field wall at Yankee Stadium, and other Japanese ads appear on the scrolling backstop advertising board. The Yankees are hoping that close ties with countries such as China and Japan will give them personal, in depth judgments of baseball talent.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, the Yankees announced a joint venture with the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> to form the basis for a partnership in running food and beverage, and other catering services to both teams\' stadiums.\n</p><p>In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine ranked New York Yankees as the fourth most valuable sports team in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> of <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> of La Liga, a value of $2.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine ranked the Yankees as the most valuable <a href="/wiki/MLB_teams" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB teams">MLB team</a> at $3.7 billion, up 9% from 2016, with the average MLB team worth $1.54 billion.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:New_York_Yankees#Poor_Quality_Sources_in_Criticism" title="Talk:New York Yankees">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Yankees&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(July 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>With the long-term success of the franchise and a large Yankee fanbase, many fans of other teams have come to dislike the Yankees.<sup id="cite_ref-suck_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suck-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The organization is sometimes referred to by detractors as "the <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Zoo" title="Bronx Zoo">Bronx Zoo</a>" (echoing the title of <a href="/wiki/Sparky_Lyle" title="Sparky Lyle">Sparky Lyle</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx_Zoo_(book)" title="The Bronx Zoo (book)">book</a>) or "the Evil Empire."<sup id="cite_ref-suck_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suck-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> When the Yankees are on the road, it is common for the home fans to chant "Yankees Suck", and T-shirts, bumper stickers and other items have been sold with this phrase.<sup id="cite_ref-suck_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suck-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the animosity toward the team may derive from its high payroll<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> (which was around $200 million at the start of the 2008 season, the highest of any American sports team),<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and the free agent superstars the team attracts in the off-season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (June 2017)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Mike_Royko" title="Mike Royko">Mike Royko</a> noted, "Hating the Yankees is as American as <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">pizza</a> pie, <a href="/wiki/Unwed_mother" class="mw-redirect" title="Unwed mother">unwed mothers</a>, and cheating on your <a href="/wiki/Income_tax_in_the_United_States" title="Income tax in the United States">income tax</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_and_theme_songs">Fight and theme songs</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:322.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/322.JPG/220px-322.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/322.JPG/330px-322.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/322.JPG/440px-322.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:322.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The grounds crew at Yankee Stadium dancing to "<a href="/wiki/Y.M.C.A._(song)" title="Y.M.C.A. (song)">Y.M.C.A.</a>"</div></div></div>\n<p>The official fight song for the Yankees is "<a href="/wiki/Here_Come_the_Yankees" title="Here Come the Yankees">Here Come the Yankees</a>", written in 1967 by Bob Bundin and Lou Stallman. While it is not used as often, it is still heard frequently in instrumental form, most prominently in radio broadcasts. Another song strongly linked to the team is "<a href="/wiki/Theme_from_New_York,_New_York" title="Theme from New York, New York">New York, New York</a>", which is played in the stadium after home games. The <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a> cover version is traditionally played after victories, and the <a href="/wiki/Liza_Minnelli" title="Liza Minnelli">Liza Minnelli</a> original version after losses. When the Yankees take the field before the start of every game, <a href="/wiki/2_Unlimited" title="2 Unlimited">2 Unlimited</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Get_Ready_For_This" class="mw-redirect" title="Get Ready For This">Get Ready For This</a>" is played, with the fans usually clapping along. When the Yankees score a run at home, a short snippet of 2 Unlimited\'s "<a href="/wiki/Workaholic_(song)" title="Workaholic (song)">Workaholic</a>" containing the bell chime of <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Quarters" title="Westminster Quarters">Westminster Quarters</a> is played (whenever Aaron Judge scores a run the snippet ends with "The Clang" tone  by veteran composer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Post" title="Mike Post">Mike Post</a>, used in the <a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order" title="Law &amp; Order">Law &amp; Order</a> franchise).\n</p><p>A wide selection of songs are played regularly at the stadium, many of them live on the Stadium\'s Hammond organ. "<a href="/wiki/God_Bless_America" title="God Bless America">God Bless America</a>" has been played during the 7th inning stretch since <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11</a>. The version typically played is an abbreviated version of <a href="/wiki/Kate_Smith" title="Kate Smith">Kate Smith</a>\'s rendition. However, during many important games (including most play-off games) and on noteworthy days, it is sung live a Capella and includes a longer introduction. During the 5th inning, the grounds crew, while performing their duties, dance to "<a href="/wiki/Y.M.C.A._(song)" title="Y.M.C.A. (song)">Y.M.C.A.</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Cotton-Eyed_Joe" title="Cotton-Eyed Joe">Cotton-Eyed Joe</a>", once played during the 7th inning stretch, is now played in the 8th inning. On the DiamondVision screen, a man in farmer\'s garb is shown dancing in the stadium\'s control room, with the words "Cotton-Eyed Joey" at the bottom. The organist will sometimes play the "<a href="/wiki/Zorbas" title="Zorbas">Zorba the Greek Theme</a>", accompanied by clapping from the audience, to excite the crowd and encourage a rally.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_broadcasters" title="List of New York Yankees broadcasters">List of New York Yankees broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/YES_Network" title="YES Network">Yankees Entertainment and Sports (YES) Network</a> launched in 2002, and serves as the primary home of the New York Yankees. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kay_(announcer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Kay (announcer)">Michael Kay</a> is the play-by-play announcer with <a href="/wiki/Ken_Singleton" title="Ken Singleton">Ken Singleton</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cone" title="David Cone">David Cone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Leiter" title="Al Leiter">Al Leiter</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Flaherty" title="John Flaherty">John Flaherty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul_O%27Neill_(baseball)" title="Paul O&#39;Neill (baseball)">Paul O\'Neill</a> working as commentators as part of a three-man, or occasionally two-man, booth. <a href="/wiki/Bob_Lorenz" title="Bob Lorenz">Bob Lorenz</a> hosts the pre-game show and the post-game show with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Curry" title="Jack Curry">Jack Curry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Meredith_Marakovits" title="Meredith Marakovits">Meredith Marakovits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Newman" class="mw-redirect" title="Nancy Newman">Nancy Newman</a> are the on-site reporters. Some games are telecast on <a href="/wiki/WPIX" title="WPIX">WPIX</a> and formerly on <a href="/wiki/WWOR-TV" title="WWOR-TV">WWOR-TV</a>; those broadcasts are produced by YES.\n</p><p>Radio broadcasts are on the <a href="/wiki/Yankees_Radio_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Yankees Radio Network">Yankees Radio Network</a>, the flagship station being <a href="/wiki/WFAN_(AM)" title="WFAN (AM)">WFAN</a> 660 AM, with <a href="/wiki/John_Sterling_(sportscaster)" title="John Sterling (sportscaster)">John Sterling</a> as the play-by-play announcer and <a href="/wiki/Suzyn_Waldman" title="Suzyn Waldman">Suzyn Waldman</a> providing the commentary, with Spanish-language broadcasts on <a href="/wiki/WADO" title="WADO">WADO</a> 1280 AM.\n</p><p>The history of Yankee radio broadcasters is: <a href="/wiki/WABC_(AM)" title="WABC (AM)">WJZ 770</a> (1939\xe2\x80\x93\'40), <a href="/wiki/WOR_(AM)" title="WOR (AM)">WOR 710</a> (1942), <a href="/wiki/WINS_(AM)" title="WINS (AM)">WINS 1010</a> (1944\xe2\x80\x93\'57), <a href="/wiki/WEPN_(AM)" title="WEPN (AM)">WMGM 1050</a> (1958\xe2\x80\x93\'60), <a href="/wiki/WCBS_(AM)" title="WCBS (AM)">WCBS 880</a> (1961\xe2\x80\x93\'66), <a href="/wiki/WEPN_(AM)" title="WEPN (AM)">WHN 1050</a> (1967\xe2\x80\x93\'70), <a href="/wiki/WMCA_(AM)" title="WMCA (AM)">WMCA 570</a> (1971\xe2\x80\x93\'77), WINS 1010 (1978\xe2\x80\x93\'80), WABC 770 (1981\xe2\x80\x932001), WCBS 880 (2002\xe2\x80\x932013), <a href="/wiki/WFAN_(AM)" title="WFAN (AM)">WFAN 660 AM</a> and <a href="/wiki/WFAN-FM" title="WFAN-FM">WFAN-FM 101.9</a> (2014\xe2\x80\x93present).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_announcers">Past announcers</span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mel_Allen" title="Mel Allen">Mel Allen</a> was the team\'s lead announcer from 1948 to 1964.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Red_Barber" title="Red Barber">Red Barber</a> called Yankees games for thirteen seasons (1954\xe2\x80\x931966).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Messer" title="Frank Messer">Frank Messer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Rizzuto" title="Phil Rizzuto">Phil Rizzuto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_White_(first_baseman)" title="Bill White (first baseman)">Bill White</a> teamed together in the 1970s and 1980s. Rizzuto, with 40 years in the broadcast booth, is the longest serving broadcaster in the history of the club. Messer and White each worked nearly two decades for the Yankees, with White notably moving on to become president of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1989. <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Murcer" title="Bobby Murcer">Bobby Murcer</a> also called games for over twenty years, and continued with the YES Network until shortly before his death from <a href="/wiki/Brain_cancer" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain cancer">brain cancer</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roster">Roster</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_coaches" title="List of New York Yankees coaches">List of New York Yankees coaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_managers" title="List of New York Yankees managers">List of New York Yankees managers</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="New York Yankees award winners and league leaders">New York Yankees award winners and league leaders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees_team_captains" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Yankees team captains">New York Yankees team captains</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_roster">Current roster</span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="7" style="background-color:#122448;color:#FFFFFF;; href="/wiki/Bernie_Williams" title="Bernie Williams">Bernie<br />Williams</a><br />CF<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap"><br />May 24, 2015</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robinson42.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robinson42.jpg/100px-Robinson42.jpg" width="100" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robinson42.jpg/150px-Robinson42.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robinson42.jpg/200px-Robinson42.jpg 2x" data-file-width="705" data-file-height="705" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie<br />Robinson</a><br />All MLB<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Honored <span style="white-space:nowrap"><br />April 15, 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The retired numbers were displayed behind the old <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>\'s left field fence and in front of the opposing team\'s bullpen, forming a little alley that connects <a href="/wiki/Monument_Park_(Yankee_Stadium)" title="Monument Park (Yankee Stadium)">Monument Park</a> to the left field stands. When the franchise moved across the street to the new stadium, the numbers were incorporated into Monument Park that sits place in center field between both bullpens. The 21 numbers are placed on the wall in chronological order, beginning with <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>\'s number 4. This was retired soon after Gehrig left baseball on July 4, 1939, the same day he gave his famous farewell speech. His was the first number retired in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> history. Beneath the numbers are plaques with the names of the players and a descriptive paragraph.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg/220px-YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg/330px-YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg/440px-YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2600" data-file-height="1950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YankeeRetiredNumbers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first four in the row of retired numbers at the old Yankee Stadium</div></div></div>\n<p>The number 42 was retired throughout Major League Baseball in honor of <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> on April 15, 1997, the 50th anniversary of his breaking the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_color_line" title="Baseball color line">color barrier</a>. The day was declared <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson_Day" title="Jackie Robinson Day">Jackie Robinson Day</a>, and was later observed by all of baseball, with select players from every team wearing the number 42. Players who wore No. 42 at the time were allowed to continue to wear it until they left the team with which they played on April 15, 1997; <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rivera" title="Mariano Rivera">Mariano Rivera</a> was the last active player covered under that <a href="/wiki/Grandfather_clause" title="Grandfather clause">grandfather clause</a>. While other teams placed the number 42 with the rest of their retired numbers, the Yankees did not do so at first. Ten years later, on April 17, 2007, the Yankees honored Robinson by mounting the logo of Jackie Robinson Day with a corresponding plaque alongside the rest of the retired numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Because the Yankees were finishing a roadtrip in Oakland on Jackie Robinson Day, the ceremony took place two days later. When the Yankees moved to the second Yankee Stadium, they replaced the Jackie Robinson Day logo with a number 42 that resembled the other retired numbers. Later on they replaced the number 42 so that it resembled the Dodger\'s style, and on September 22, 2013, a plaque was dedicated to Robinson in Monument Park. Also, the number 42 dedicated to Robinson was removed entirely and replaced with one for Mariano Rivera.\n</p><p>In 1972, the number 8 was retired for two players on the same day, in honor of catcher <a href="/wiki/Bill_Dickey" title="Bill Dickey">Bill Dickey</a> and his protege, catcher <a href="/wiki/Yogi_Berra" title="Yogi Berra">Yogi Berra</a>. Berra inherited Dickey\'s number in 1948 after Dickey ended his playing career and became a coach.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Billy_Martin" title="Billy Martin">Billy Martin</a> is the only Yankee to have his number retired as a player/manager combination. He wore number 1 as a player in the 1950s and as a manager in the 1970s and 1980s.\n</p><p>The numbers 37 and 6, retired for <a href="/wiki/Casey_Stengel" title="Casey Stengel">Casey Stengel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a> respectively, are the only numbers retired by the Yankees for someone who served solely as manager of the team. Stengel managed the Yankees to ten pennants and seven world championships between 1949 and 1960, including a record five consecutive world championships from 1949 through 1953. Joe Torre managed the Yankees from 1996 to 2007, winning six pennants and four World Series championships.\n</p><p>On May 14, 2017, the Yankees retired number 2 in honor of Derek Jeter.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> This leaves 0, which the Yankees have never issued in their history, as the only single-digit number available for future Yankees.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Brett Gardner, as of July 2018 the Yankees\' longest tenured player, wears the smallest number on their active roster, number 11.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hall_of_Famers">Hall of Famers</span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%; margin: 1em
