due to playing at a time when caps bore no insignia.</li>\n<li>** Catfish Hunter could not decide between the Yankees and Athletics, and so opted to wear no insignia on his cap upon his induction.</li>\n<li><sup>\xe2\x80\xa0</sup> Larry MacPhail served as co-owner, president and general manager of the Yankees.  Lee MacPhail served as director of player personnel and general manager of the Yankees.  Both were inducted as Executives by the Veterans Committee. Neither were affiliated with a primary team or depicted on their plaques with caps</li>\n<li><sup>\xe2\x80\xa1</sup> Jacob Ruppert was inducted as an Executive/Pioneer for his contributions to baseball as owner of the Yankees. Ed Barrow and George Weiss were inducted as Executives for their work as general managers of the Yankees.  They are depicted on their plaques without caps.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%; margin: 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color: #122448; color: #FFFFFF; text-align: center;">New York Yankees <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boston_Red_Sox">Boston Red Sox</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yankees%E2%80%93Red_Sox_rivalry" title="Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry">Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry is one of the oldest, most famous and fiercest <a href="/wiki/List_of_sports_rivalries" title="List of sports rivalries">rivalries in professional sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FiercestRivalry_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FiercestRivalry-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StrongestRivalry_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StrongestRivalry-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UltimateRivalry_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UltimateRivalry-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> For over 100 years, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> and the Yankees have been intense rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-Enemies_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enemies-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The rivalry is often termed "the best"<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and "greatest rivalry in all of sports."<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Games between the two teams are often broadcast on national television, schedule permitting.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rivalry is sometimes so polarizing that it is often a heated subject, like religion or politics, in the Northeastern United States.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Since the inception of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> team and an added Division Series, the <a href="/wiki/American_League_East" title="American League East">American League East</a> rivals have squared off in the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> three times, with the Yankees winning twice in <a href="/wiki/1999_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1999 American League Championship Series">1999</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2003 American League Championship Series">2003</a> and the Sox winning in <a href="/wiki/2004_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2004 American League Championship Series">2004</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ALCS_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALCS-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the teams have twice met in the last regular-season series of a season to decide the league title, in 1904 (when the Red Sox won) and 1949 (when the Yankees won).<sup id="cite_ref-ALCS_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALCS-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The teams also finished tied for first in 1978, when the Yankees won a high-profile <a href="/wiki/1978_American_League_East_tie-breaker_game" title="1978 American League East tie-breaker game">one-game playoff</a> for the division title.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The 1978 division race is memorable for the Red Sox having held a 14-game lead over the Yankees more than halfway through the season.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, the 2004 ALCS is notable for the Yankees leading 3 games to 0 and ultimately losing a best of seven series.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The Red Sox comeback was the only time in baseball history that a team has come back from a 0\xe2\x80\x933 deficit to win a postseason series.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subway_Series">Subway Series</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mets%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Mets\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Mets\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giants%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Giants\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Giants\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Subway Series is a series of games played between teams based in New York City.  The term\'s historic usage has been in reference to <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> games played between New York teams.  The Yankees have appeared in all Subway Series games as they have been the only <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> team in the city, and have compiled an 11\xe2\x80\x933 record in the fourteen championship Subway Series. Since 1997, the term Subway Series has also been applied to <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> during the regular season between the Yankees and <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_minor_league_affiliates" title="List of New York Yankees minor league affiliates">List of New York Yankees minor league affiliates</a></div>\n<p>The Yankees are affiliated with the following minor league teams:<sup id="cite_ref-minorleagues_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorleagues-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="mw-headline" id="Front_office">Front office</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_owners_and_executives" title="List of New York Yankees owners and executives">List of New York Yankees owners and executives</a></div>\n<p>The Yankees front office, as of 2013, included <a href="/wiki/Hal_Steinbrenner" title="Hal Steinbrenner">Hal Steinbrenner</a> (Managing General Partner/Co-Chairperson), <a href="/wiki/Randy_Levine" title="Randy Levine">Randy Levine</a> (President), Lonn A. Trost (Chief Operating Officer and General Counsel), and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cashman" title="Brian Cashman">Brian Cashman</a> (Senior Vice President, General Manager).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Yankees_managers" title="List of New York Yankees managers">List of New York Yankees managers</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pressbox.mlb.com/pressbox/downloads/y2018/2018_NYY_Media_Guide.pdf#page=251">"History of the Yankees Uniform &amp; NY Logo"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>2018 New York Yankees Official Media Guide &amp; Record Book</i>. <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a>.
